       Miscalculated macroeconomic decisions, a
       <a href="/wiki/Finnish_banking_crisis_of_1990s" title="Finnish banking crisis of 1990s">
        banking crisis
       </a>
       , the collapse of its largest single trading partner (the Soviet Union), and a global economic downturn caused a deep
       <a href="/wiki/Early_1990s_depression_in_Finland" title="Early 1990s depression in Finland">
        early 1990s recession in Finland
       </a>
       . The depression bottomed out in 1993, and Finland saw steady economic growth for more than ten years.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Like other Nordic countries, Finland decentralised its economy since the late 1980s. Financial and product market regulation were loosened. Some state enterprises have been privatized and there have been some modest tax cuts.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Finland joined the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
        European Union
       </a>
       in 1995, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">
        Eurozone
       </a>
       in 1999. Much of the late 1990s economic growth was fueled by the phenomenal success of the mobile phone manufacturer
       <a href="/wiki/Nokia" title="Nokia">
        Nokia
       </a>
       , which held a unique position of representing 80% of the market capitalization of the
       <a href="/wiki/Helsinki_Stock_Exchange" title="Helsinki Stock Exchange">
        Helsinki Stock Exchange
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Language">
        Language
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Language">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Finnish_language" title="Finnish language">
        Finnish language
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Finland_Swedish" title="Finland Swedish">
        Finland Swedish
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Finland" title="Languages of Finland">
        Languages of Finland
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Finnish and
       <a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">
        Swedish
       </a>
       are the official languages of Finland. Finnish predominates nationwide while Swedish is spoken in some coastal areas in the west and south and in the autonomous region of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C3%85land" title="Åland">
        Åland
       </a>
       . The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_language" title="Native language">
        native language
       </a>
       of 89% of the population is Finnish,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Population_according_to_language_59-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Population_according_to_language-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which is part of the Finnic subgroup of the Uralic languages. The language is one of only four official
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_European_Union" title="Languages of the European Union">
        EU languages
       </a>
       not of
       <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">
        Indo-European
       </a>
       origin. Finnish is closely related to
       <a href="/wiki/Karelian_language" title="Karelian language">
        Karelian
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Estonian_language" title="Estonian language">
        Estonian
       </a>
       and more remotely to the Sami languages and
       <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">
        Hungarian
       </a>
       . Swedish is the native language of 5.3% of the population (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swedish-speaking_Finns" title="Swedish-speaking Finns">
        Swedish-speaking Finns
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-population-2016_60-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-population-2016-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Nordic_countries" title="Nordic countries">
        Nordic
       </a>
       languages and
       <a href="/wiki/Karelian_language" title="Karelian language">
        Karelian
       </a>
       are also specially treated in some contexts.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Finnish_Kalo_language" title="Finnish Kalo language">
        Finnish Romani
       </a>
       is spoken by some 5,000–6,000 people,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kalo_Finnish_Romani_language" title="Kalo Finnish Romani language">
        Finnish Romani
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Finnish_Sign_Language" title="Finnish Sign Language">
        Finnish Sign Language
       </a>
       are also recognized in the constitution. There are two sign languages:
       <a href="/wiki/Finnish_Sign_Language" title="Finnish Sign Language">
        Finnish Sign Language
       </a>
       , spoken natively by 4,000–5,000 people,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Finland-Swedish_Sign_Language" title="Finland-Swedish Sign Language">
        Finland-Swedish Sign Language
       </a>
       , spoken natively by about 150 people. Tatar language is spoken by a
       <a href="/wiki/Finnish_Tatars" title="Finnish Tatars">
        Finnish Tatar
       </a>
       minority of about 800 people who moved to Finland mainly during the Russian rule from the 1870s until the 1920s.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Sami_languages" title="Sami languages">
        Sami language
       </a>
       is an official language to the north, in Lapland or in northern Lapland, where are the Sami people, numbering around 7,000
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and recognized as an
       <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">
        indigenous people
       </a>
       . About a quarter of them speak a
       <a href="/wiki/Sami_languages" title="Sami languages">
        Sami language
       </a>
       as their mother tongue.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Population_2006-12-31_64-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Population_2006-12-31-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Sami languages that are spoken in Finland are
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Sami" title="Northern Sami">
        Northern Sami
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Inari_Sami_language" title="Inari Sami language">
        Inari Sami
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Skolt_Sami_language" title="Skolt Sami language">
        Skolt Sami
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [note 1]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The rights of minority groups (in particular
       <a href="/wiki/Sami_people#Finland" title="Sami people">
        Sami
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Swedish-speaking_population_of_Finland" title="Swedish-speaking population of Finland">
        Swedish speakers
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Finnish_Kale" title="Finnish Kale">
        Romani people
       </a>
       ) are protected by the constitution.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The largest immigrant languages are Russian (1.4%), Estonian (0.9%), Arabic (0.4%), Somali (0.3%) and English (0.3%).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-population-2016_60-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-population-2016-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       English is studied by most pupils as a compulsory subject from the third or fifth grade (at 9 or 11 years of age respectively) in the comprehensive school (in some schools other languages can be chosen instead). German, French, and Russian can be studied as second foreign languages from the eighth grade (at 14 years of age; some schools may offer other options).
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Geography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Finland" title="Geography of Finland">
        Geography of Finland
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Finland" title="List of cities and towns in Finland">
        List of cities and towns in Finland
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_lakes_in_Finland" title="List of lakes in Finland">
        List of lakes in Finland
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_parks_of_Finland" title="List of national parks of Finland">
        List of national parks of Finland
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Environmental_issues_in_Finland" title="Environmental issues in Finland">
        Environmental issues in Finland
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Lying approximately between latitudes
       <a href="/wiki/60th_parallel_north" title="60th parallel north">
        60°
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/70th_parallel_north" title="70th parallel north">
        70° N
       </a>
       , and longitudes
       <a href="/wiki/20th_meridian_east" title="20th meridian east">
        20°
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/32nd_meridian_east" title="32nd meridian east">
        32° E
       </a>
       , Finland is one of the world's northernmost countries. Of world capitals, only
       <a href="/wiki/Reykjav%C3%ADk" title="Reykjavík">
        Reykjavík
       </a>
       lies more to the north than
       <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">
        Helsinki
       </a>
       . The distance from the southernmost point –
       <a href="/wiki/Hanko" title="Hanko">
        Hanko
       </a>
       in Uusimaa – to the northernmost –
       <a href="/wiki/Nuorgam" title="Nuorgam">
        Nuorgam
       </a>
       in Lapland – is 1,160 kilometres (720 mi).
      </p>
      <p>
       Finland has about 168,000 lakes (of area larger than 500 m
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       or 0.12 acres) and 179,000 islands.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Its largest lake,
       <a href="/wiki/Saimaa" title="Saimaa">
        Saimaa
       </a>
       , is the fourth largest in Europe. The
       <a href="/wiki/Finnish_Lakeland" title="Finnish Lakeland">
        Finnish Lakeland
       </a>
       is the area with the most lakes in the country. The greatest concentration of islands is found in the southwest, in the
       <a href="/wiki/Archipelago_Sea" title="Archipelago Sea">
        Archipelago Sea
       </a>
       between continental Finland and the main island of Åland.
      </p>
      <p>
       Much of the geography of Finland is a result of the Ice Age. The glaciers were thicker and lasted longer in
       <a href="/wiki/Fennoscandia" title="Fennoscandia">
        Fennoscandia
       </a>
       compared with the rest of Europe. Their eroding effects have left the Finnish landscape mostly flat with few hills and fewer mountains. Its highest point, the
       <a href="/wiki/Halti" title="Halti">
        Halti
       </a>
       at 1,324 metres (4,344 ft), is found in the extreme north of Lapland at the border between Finland and
       <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">
        Norway
       </a>
       . The highest mountain whose peak is entirely in Finland is
       <a href="/wiki/Ridnit%C5%A1ohkka" title="Ridnitšohkka">
        Ridnitšohkka
       </a>
       at 1,316 m (4,318 ft), directly adjacent to Halti.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cygnus_cygnus_from_zh.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="682" data-file-width="909" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Cygnus_cygnus_from_zh.JPG/220px-Cygnus_cygnus_from_zh.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Cygnus_cygnus_from_zh.JPG/330px-Cygnus_cygnus_from_zh.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Cygnus_cygnus_from_zh.JPG/440px-Cygnus_cygnus_from_zh.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cygnus_cygnus_from_zh.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Whooper_swan" title="Whooper swan">
          whooper swan
         </a>
         , Finland's
         <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_birds" title="List of national birds">
          national bird
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The retreating glaciers have left the land with
       <a href="/wiki/Moraine" title="Moraine">
        morainic
       </a>
       deposits in formations of
       <a href="/wiki/Esker" title="Esker">
        eskers
       </a>
       . These are ridges of stratified gravel and sand, running northwest to southeast, where the ancient edge of the glacier once lay. Among the biggest of these are the three
       <a href="/wiki/Salpausselk%C3%A4" title="Salpausselkä">
        Salpausselkä
       </a>
       ridges that run across southern Finland.
      </p>
      <p>
       Having been compressed under the enormous weight of the glaciers, terrain in Finland is rising due to the
       <a href="/wiki/Post-glacial_rebound" title="Post-glacial rebound">
        post-glacial rebound
       </a>
       . The effect is strongest around the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Bothnia" title="Gulf of Bothnia">
        Gulf of Bothnia
       </a>
       , where land steadily rises about 1 cm (0.4 in) a year. As a result, the old sea bottom turns little by little into dry land: the surface area of the country is expanding by about 7 square kilometres (2.7 sq mi) annually.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Relatively speaking, Finland is rising from the sea.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB_69-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-EB-69">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The landscape is covered mostly by coniferous
       <a href="/wiki/Taiga" title="Taiga">
        taiga
       </a>
       forests and
       <a href="/wiki/Fen" title="Fen">
        fens
       </a>
       , with little cultivated land. Of the total area 10% is lakes, rivers and ponds, and 78% forest. The forest consists of
       <a href="/wiki/Pine" title="Pine">
        pine
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Spruce" title="Spruce">
        spruce
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Birch" title="Birch">
        birch
       </a>
       , and other species.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Finland is the largest producer of wood in Europe and among the largest in the world. The most common type of rock is
       <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">
        granite
       </a>
       . It is a ubiquitous part of the scenery, visible wherever there is no soil cover. Moraine or
       <a href="/wiki/Till" title="Till">
        till
       </a>
       is the most common type of soil, covered by a thin layer of
       <a href="/wiki/Humus" title="Humus">
        humus
       </a>
       of biological origin.
       <a href="/wiki/Podzol" title="Podzol">
        Podzol
       </a>
       profile development is seen in most forest soils except where drainage is poor.
       <a href="/wiki/Gleysol" title="Gleysol">
        Gleysols
       </a>
       and peat
       <a href="/wiki/Bog" title="Bog">
        bogs
       </a>
       occupy poorly drained areas.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">
        Biodiversity
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Fauna_of_Finland" title="Fauna of Finland">
        Fauna of Finland
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Finland" title="Wildlife of Finland">
        Wildlife of Finland
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Phytogeography" title="Phytogeography">
        Phytogeographically
       </a>
       , Finland is shared between the Arctic, central European, and northern European provinces of the
       <a href="/wiki/Circumboreal_Region" title="Circumboreal Region">
        Circumboreal Region
       </a>
       within the
       <a href="/wiki/Boreal_Kingdom" title="Boreal Kingdom">
        Boreal Kingdom
       </a>
       . According to the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Fund_for_Nature" title="World Wide Fund for Nature">
        WWF
       </a>
       , the territory of Finland can be subdivided into three
       <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">
        ecoregions
       </a>
       : the
       <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_and_Russian_taiga" title="Scandinavian and Russian taiga">
        Scandinavian and Russian taiga
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sarmatic_mixed_forests" title="Sarmatic mixed forests">
        Sarmatic mixed forests
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Montane_Birch_forest_and_grasslands" title="Scandinavian Montane Birch forest and grasslands">
        Scandinavian Montane Birch forest and grasslands
       </a>
       . Taiga covers most of Finland from northern regions of southern provinces to the north of Lapland. On the southwestern coast, south of the Helsinki-
       <a href="/wiki/Rauma,_Finland" title="Rauma, Finland">
        Rauma
       </a>
       line, forests are characterized by mixed forests, that are more typical in the Baltic region. In the extreme north of Finland, near the
       <a href="/wiki/Tree_line" title="Tree line">
        tree line
       </a>
       and Arctic Ocean, Montane Birch forests are common.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bear_Finland.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1366" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Bear_Finland.png/220px-Bear_Finland.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Bear_Finland.png/330px-Bear_Finland.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Bear_Finland.png/440px-Bear_Finland.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bear_Finland.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Brown_bear" title="Brown bear">
          brown bear
         </a>
         (
         <i>
          Ursus arctos
         </i>
         ) is Finland's national animal.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Similarly, Finland has a diverse and extensive range of fauna. There are at least sixty native
       <a href="/wiki/Mammal" title="Mammal">
        mammalian
       </a>
       species, 248 breeding bird species, over 70 fish species, and 11 reptile and frog species present today, many migrating from neighboring countries thousands of years ago. Large and widely recognized wildlife mammals found in Finland are the
       <a href="/wiki/Brown_bear" title="Brown bear">
        brown bear
       </a>
       (the national animal),
       <a href="/wiki/Gray_wolf" title="Gray wolf">
        gray wolf
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Wolverine" title="Wolverine">
        wolverine
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Moose" title="Moose">
        elk
       </a>
       . Three of the more striking birds are the
       <a href="/wiki/Whooper_swan" title="Whooper swan">
        whooper swan
       </a>
       , a large European swan and the national bird of Finland; the
       <a href="/wiki/Western_capercaillie" title="Western capercaillie">
        Western capercaillie
       </a>
       , a large, black-plumaged member of the
       <a href="/wiki/Grouse" title="Grouse">
        grouse
       </a>
       family; and the
       <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_eagle-owl" title="Eurasian eagle-owl">
        Eurasian eagle-owl
       </a>
       . The latter is considered an indicator of
       <a href="/wiki/Old-growth_forest" title="Old-growth forest">
        old-growth forest
       </a>
       connectivity, and has been declining because of landscape fragmentation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
        <a href="#cite_note-71">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The most common breeding birds are the
       <a href="/wiki/Willow_warbler" title="Willow warbler">
        willow warbler
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Common_chaffinch" title="Common chaffinch">
        common chaffinch
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Redwing" title="Redwing">
        redwing
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Of some seventy species of freshwater fish, the
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_pike" title="Northern pike">
        northern pike
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Perch" title="Perch">
        perch
       </a>
       , and others are plentiful.
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_salmon" title="Atlantic salmon">
        Atlantic salmon
       </a>
       remains the favourite of
       <a href="/wiki/Fly_fishing" title="Fly fishing">
        fly rod
       </a>
       enthusiasts.
      </p>
      <p>
       The endangered
       <a href="/wiki/Saimaa_ringed_seal" title="Saimaa ringed seal">
        Saimaa ringed seal
       </a>
       , one of only three lake seal species in the world, exists only in the
       <a href="/wiki/Saimaa" title="Saimaa">
        Saimaa
       </a>
       lake system of southeastern Finland, down to only 300 seals today. It has become the emblem of the Finnish Association for Nature Conservation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
        <a href="#cite_note-73">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Climate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Finland" title="Climate of Finland">
        Climate of Finland
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Finland_koppen.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1773" data-file-width="765" height="510" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Finland_koppen.svg/220px-Finland_koppen.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Finland_koppen.svg/330px-Finland_koppen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Finland_koppen.svg/440px-Finland_koppen.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Finland_koppen.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">
          Köppen climate classification
         </a>
         types of Finland
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Koli_National_Park_in_Northern_Karelia.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2322" data-file-width="4128" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Koli_National_Park_in_Northern_Karelia.jpg/220px-Koli_National_Park_in_Northern_Karelia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Koli_National_Park_in_Northern_Karelia.jpg/330px-Koli_National_Park_in_Northern_Karelia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Koli_National_Park_in_Northern_Karelia.jpg/440px-Koli_National_Park_in_Northern_Karelia.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Koli_National_Park_in_Northern_Karelia.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Koli_National_Park" title="Koli National Park">
          Koli National Park
         </a>
         in North Karelia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Repoveden_Kansallispuisto_Kesayonauringossa.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="616" data-file-width="1024" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Repoveden_Kansallispuisto_Kesayonauringossa.jpg/220px-Repoveden_Kansallispuisto_Kesayonauringossa.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Repoveden_Kansallispuisto_Kesayonauringossa.jpg/330px-Repoveden_Kansallispuisto_Kesayonauringossa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Repoveden_Kansallispuisto_Kesayonauringossa.jpg/440px-Repoveden_Kansallispuisto_Kesayonauringossa.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Repoveden_Kansallispuisto_Kesayonauringossa.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Repovesi_National_Park" title="Repovesi National Park">
          Repovesi National Park
         </a>
         in southeastern Finland
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The main factor influencing Finland's climate is the country's geographical position between the 60th and 70th northern parallels in the
       <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">
        Eurasian
       </a>
       continent's coastal zone. In the
       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">
        Köppen climate classification
       </a>
       , the whole of Finland lies in the
       <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">
        boreal zone
       </a>
       , characterized by warm summers and freezing winters. Within the country, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Temperateness" title="Temperateness">
        temperateness
       </a>
       varies considerably between the southern coastal regions and the extreme north, showing characteristics of both a
       <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">
        maritime
       </a>
       and a
       <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">
        continental climate
       </a>
       . Finland is near enough to the Atlantic Ocean to be continuously warmed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">
        Gulf Stream
       </a>
       . The Gulf Stream combines with the moderating effects of the
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">
        Baltic Sea
       </a>
       and numerous inland lakes to explain the unusually warm climate compared with other regions that share the same
       <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">
        latitude
       </a>
       , such as
       <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">
        Alaska
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">
        Siberia
       </a>
       , and southern
       <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">
        Greenland
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Finland's_climate_74-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Finland's_climate-74">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Winters in southern Finland (when mean daily temperature remains below 0 °C or 32 °F) are usually about 100 days long, and in the inland the snow typically covers the land from about late November to April, and on the coastal areas such as
       <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">
        Helsinki
       </a>
       , snow often covers the land from late December to late March.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
        <a href="#cite_note-75">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Even in the south, the harshest winter nights can see the temperatures fall to −30 °C (−22 °F) although on coastal areas like Helsinki, temperatures below −30 °C (−22 °F) are very rare. Climatic summers (when mean daily temperature remains above 10 °C or 50 °F) in southern Finland last from about late May to mid-September, and in the inland, the warmest days of July can reach over 35 °C (95 °F).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Finland's_climate_74-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Finland's_climate-74">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Although most of Finland lies on the
       <a href="/wiki/Taiga" title="Taiga">
        taiga
       </a>
       belt, the southernmost coastal regions are sometimes classified as
       <a href="/wiki/Hemiboreal" title="Hemiboreal">
        hemiboreal
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Havas_76-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Havas-76">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Isokuru.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="780" data-file-width="1040" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Isokuru.JPG/220px-Isokuru.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Isokuru.JPG/330px-Isokuru.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Isokuru.JPG/440px-Isokuru.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Isokuru.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Pyh%C3%A4-Luosto_National_Park" title="Pyhä-Luosto National Park">
          Pyhä-Luosto National Park
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Lapland_(Finland)" title="Lapland (Finland)">
          Lapland
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In northern Finland, particularly in Lapland, the winters are long and cold, while the summers are relatively warm but short. The most severe winter days in Lapland can see the temperature fall down to −45 °C (−49 °F). The winter of the north lasts for about 200 days with permanent snow cover from about mid-October to early May. Summers in the north are quite short, only two to three months, but can still see maximum daily temperatures above 25 °C (77 °F) during heat waves.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Finland's_climate_74-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Finland's_climate-74">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       No part of Finland has
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arctic_tundra" title="Arctic tundra">
        Arctic tundra
       </a>
       , but
       <a href="/wiki/Alpine_tundra" title="Alpine tundra">
        Alpine tundra
       </a>
       can be found at the
       <a href="/wiki/Fell" title="Fell">
        fells
       </a>
       Lapland.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Havas_76-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Havas-76">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Finnish climate is suitable for cereal farming only in the southernmost regions, while the northern regions are suitable for
       <a href="/wiki/Animal_husbandry" title="Animal husbandry">
        animal husbandry
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A quarter of Finland's territory lies within the
       <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Circle" title="Arctic Circle">
        Arctic Circle
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Midnight_sun" title="Midnight sun">
        midnight sun
       </a>
       can be experienced for more days the farther north one travels. At Finland's northernmost point, the sun does not set for 73 consecutive days during summer, and does not rise at all for 51 days during winter.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Finland's_climate_74-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Finland's_climate-74">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Regions">
        Regions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Regions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Finland" title="Regions of Finland">
        Regions of Finland
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Finland consists of 19
       <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Finland" title="Regions of Finland">
        regions
       </a>
       called
       <i>
        <span lang="fi">
         <b>
          maakunta
         </b>
        </span>
       </i>
       in Finnish and
       <i>
        <span lang="sv">
         <b>
          landskap
         </b>
        </span>
       </i>
       in Swedish. The regions are governed by regional councils which serve as forums of cooperation for the
       <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Finland" title="Municipalities of Finland">
        municipalities
       </a>
       of a region. The main tasks of the regions are regional planning and development of enterprise and education. In addition, the public health services are usually organized on the basis of regions. Currently, the only region where a popular election is held for the council is Kainuu. Other regional councils are elected by municipal councils, each municipality sending representatives in proportion to its population.
      </p>
      <p>
       In addition to inter-municipal cooperation, which is the responsibility of regional councils, each region has a state Employment and Economic Development Centre which is responsible for the local administration of labour, agriculture, fisheries, forestry, and entrepreneurial affairs. The
       <a href="/wiki/Finnish_Defence_Forces" title="Finnish Defence Forces">
        Finnish Defence Forces
       </a>
       regional offices are responsible for the regional defence preparations and for the administration of conscription within the region.
      </p>
      <p>
       Regions represent dialectal, cultural, and economic variations better than the former
       <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Finland" title="Provinces of Finland">
        provinces
       </a>
       , which were purely administrative divisions of the central government. Historically, regions are divisions of
       <a href="/wiki/Historical_provinces_of_Finland" title="Historical provinces of Finland">
        historical provinces of Finland
       </a>
       , areas which represent dialects and culture more accurately.
      </p>
      <p>
       Six
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Regional_State_Administrative_Agencies_of_Finland" title="Regional State Administrative Agencies of Finland">
        Regional State Administrative Agencies
       </a>
       were created by the state of Finland in 2010, each of them responsible for one of the regions called
       <i>
        <span lang="fi">
         <i>
          alue
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       in Finnish and
       <i>
        <span lang="sv">
         <i>
          region
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       in Swedish; in addition, Åland was designated a seventh region. These take over some of the tasks of the earlier
       <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Finland" title="Provinces of Finland">
        Provinces of Finland
       </a>
       (the
       <i>
        lääni
       </i>
       s), which were abolished.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
        <a href="#cite_note-78">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <p>
       The region of
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Uusimaa" title="Eastern Uusimaa">
        Eastern Uusimaa
       </a>
       was consolidated with Uusimaa on 1 January 2011.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
        <a href="#cite_note-80">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">
        Administrative divisions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Finland" title="Administrative divisions of Finland">
        Administrative divisions of Finland
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Finland" title="Regions of Finland">
        Regions of Finland
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sub-regions_of_Finland" title="Sub-regions of Finland">
        Sub-regions of Finland
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Finland" title="Municipalities of Finland">
        Municipalities of Finland
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Historical_provinces_of_Finland" title="Historical provinces of Finland">
        Historical provinces of Finland
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Finnish_municipalities" title="List of Finnish municipalities">
        List of Finnish municipalities
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Finnish_municipalities_by_population" title="List of Finnish municipalities by population">
        List of Finnish municipalities by population
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Finnish_municipalities_by_area" title="List of Finnish municipalities by area">
        List of Finnish municipalities by area
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Former_municipalities_of_Finland" title="Former municipalities of Finland">
        Former municipalities of Finland
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The fundamental administrative divisions of the country are the
       <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Finland" title="Municipalities of Finland">
        municipalities
       </a>
       , which may also call themselves towns or cities. They account for half of public spending. Spending is financed by municipal income tax, state subsidies, and other revenue. As of 2017
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , there are 311 municipalities,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Suomen_Kuntaliitto_9-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Suomen_Kuntaliitto-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and most have fewer than 6,000 residents.
      </p>
      <p>
       In addition to municipalities, two intermediate levels are defined. Municipalities co-operate in seventy
       <a href="/wiki/Sub-regions_of_Finland" title="Sub-regions of Finland">
        sub-regions
       </a>
       and nineteen
       <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Finland" title="Regions of Finland">
        regions
       </a>
       . These are governed by the member municipalities and have only limited powers. The autonomous province of Åland has a permanent democratically elected regional council. Sami people have a semi-autonomous
       <a href="/wiki/Sami_native_region_(Finland)" title="Sami native region (Finland)">
        Sami native region
       </a>
       in Lapland for issues on language and culture.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the following chart, the number of inhabitants includes those living in the entire municipality (
       <i>
        kunta/kommun
       </i>
       ), not just in the built-up area. The land area is given in km², and the density in inhabitants per km² (land area). The figures are as of 31 August 2017. The
       <a href="/wiki/Capital_region" title="Capital region">
        capital region
       </a>
       – comprising
       <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">
        Helsinki
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Vantaa" title="Vantaa">
        Vantaa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Espoo" title="Espoo">
        Espoo
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Kauniainen" title="Kauniainen">
        Kauniainen
       </a>
       – forms a continuous
       <a href="/wiki/Conurbation" title="Conurbation">
        conurbation
       </a>
       of over 1.1 million people. However, common administration is limited to voluntary cooperation of all municipalities, e.g. in
       <a href="/wiki/Helsinki_Metropolitan_Area_Council" title="Helsinki Metropolitan Area Council">
        Helsinki Metropolitan Area Council
       </a>
       .
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">
        Politics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Politics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Finland" title="Politics of Finland">
        Politics of Finland
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Finland" title="List of political parties in Finland">
        List of political parties in Finland
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Finland" title="Human rights in Finland">
        Human rights in Finland
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Constitution">
        Constitution
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Constitution">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Finland" title="Constitution of Finland">
        Constitution of Finland
       </a>
       defines the political system; Finland is a
       <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">
        parliamentary republic
       </a>
       within the framework of a
       <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">
        representative democracy
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Finland" title="Prime Minister of Finland">
        Prime Minister
       </a>
       is the country's most powerful person. The current version of the constitution was enacted on 1 March 2000, and was amended on 1 March 2012. Citizens can run and vote in parliamentary, municipal, presidential and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elections_in_the_European_Union" title="Elections in the European Union">
        European Union elections
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="President">
        President
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: President">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/President_of_Finland" title="President of Finland">
        President of Finland
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">
        head of state
       </a>
       of Finland is
       <a href="/wiki/President_of_Finland" title="President of Finland">
        President of the Republic of Finland
       </a>
       (in Finnish:
       <i>
        Suomen tasavallan presidentti
       </i>
       ; in Swedish:
       <i>
        Republiken Finlands president
       </i>
       ). Finland has had for most of its independence a
       <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">
        semi-presidential system
       </a>
       , but in the last few decades the powers of the President have been diminished. In constitution amendments, which came into effect in 1991 or 1992 and also with a new drafted constitution of 2000, amended in 2012, the President's position has become primarily a ceremonial office. However, the President still leads the nation's foreign politics together with the Council of State and is the chief-in-command of the Defence Forces.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Parliamentary_1-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Parliamentary-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The position still does entail some powers, including responsibility for
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Finland" title="Foreign relations of Finland">
        foreign policy
       </a>
       (excluding affairs related to the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
        European Union
       </a>
       ) in cooperation with the
       <a href="/wiki/Finnish_Government" title="Finnish Government">
        cabinet
       </a>
       , being
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commander-in-Chief" title="Commander-in-Chief">
        the head of the armed forces
       </a>
       , some decree powers, and some appointive powers. Direct, one- or two-stage elections are used to elect the president for a term of six years and for a maximum of two consecutive terms. The current president is
       <a href="/wiki/Sauli_Niinist%C3%B6" title="Sauli Niinistö">
        Sauli Niinistö
       </a>
       ; he took office on 1 March 2012. Former presidents were
       <a href="/wiki/Kaarlo_Juho_St%C3%A5hlberg" title="Kaarlo Juho Ståhlberg">
        K. J. Ståhlberg
       </a>
       (1919–1925),
       <a href="/wiki/Lauri_Kristian_Relander" title="Lauri Kristian Relander">
        L. K. Relander
       </a>
       (1925–1931),
       <a href="/wiki/Pehr_Evind_Svinhufvud" title="Pehr Evind Svinhufvud">
        P. E. Svinhufvud
       </a>
       (1931–1937),
       <a href="/wiki/Ky%C3%B6sti_Kallio" title="Kyösti Kallio">
        Kyösti Kallio
       </a>
       (1937–1940),
       <a href="/wiki/Risto_Ryti" title="Risto Ryti">
        Risto Ryti
       </a>
       (1940–1944),
       <a href="/wiki/Carl_Gustaf_Emil_Mannerheim" title="Carl Gustaf Emil Mannerheim">
        C. G. E. Mannerheim
       </a>
       (1944–1946),
       <a href="/wiki/Juho_Kusti_Paasikivi" title="Juho Kusti Paasikivi">
        J. K. Paasikivi
       </a>
       (1946–1956),
       <a href="/wiki/Urho_Kekkonen" title="Urho Kekkonen">
        Urho Kekkonen
       </a>
       (1956–1982),
       <a href="/wiki/Mauno_Koivisto" title="Mauno Koivisto">
        Mauno Koivisto
       </a>
       (1982–1994),
       <a href="/wiki/Martti_Ahtisaari" title="Martti Ahtisaari">
        Martti Ahtisaari
       </a>
       (1994–2000), and
       <a href="/wiki/Tarja_Halonen" title="Tarja Halonen">
        Tarja Halonen
       </a>
       (2000–2012).
      </p>
      <p>
       The current president was elected from the ranks of the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Coalition_Party" title="National Coalition Party">
        National Coalition Party
       </a>
       for the first time since 1946. The presidency between 1946 and the present was instead held by a member of the
       <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Finland" title="Social Democratic Party of Finland">
        Social Democratic Party
       </a>
       or the
       <a href="/wiki/Centre_Party_(Finland)" title="Centre Party (Finland)">
        Centre Party
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Parliament">
        Parliament
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Parliament">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Finland" title="Parliament of Finland">
        Parliament of Finland
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Eduskuntatalo_Helsinki.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2731" data-file-width="3643" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Eduskuntatalo_Helsinki.jpg/220px-Eduskuntatalo_Helsinki.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Eduskuntatalo_Helsinki.jpg/330px-Eduskuntatalo_Helsinki.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Eduskuntatalo_Helsinki.jpg/440px-Eduskuntatalo_Helsinki.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Eduskuntatalo_Helsinki.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Finland" title="Parliament of Finland">
          Parliament of Finland
         </a>
         's main building.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The 200-member
       <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">
        unicameral
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Finland" title="Parliament of Finland">
        Parliament of Finland
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Finnish_language" title="Finnish language">
        Finnish
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="fi">
         Eduskunta
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">
        Swedish
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="sv">
         Riksdag
        </span>
       </i>
       ) exercises supreme legislative authority in the country. It may alter the constitution and ordinary laws, dismiss the cabinet, and override presidential vetoes. Its acts are not subject to judicial review; the constitutionality of new laws is assessed by the parliament's
       <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Finland#Committees" title="Parliament of Finland">
        constitutional law committee
       </a>
       . The parliament is elected for a term of four years using the proportional
       <a href="/wiki/D%27Hondt_method" title="D'Hondt method">
        D'Hondt method
       </a>
       within a number of multi-seat constituencies through open list multi-member districts. Various parliament committees listen to experts and prepare legislation. The
       <a href="/wiki/Speaker_of_the_Parliament_of_Finland" title="Speaker of the Parliament of Finland">
        speaker of the parliament
       </a>
       is
       <a href="/wiki/Maria_Lohela" title="Maria Lohela">
        Maria Lohela
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Blue_Reform" title="Blue Reform">
        sin.
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Since
       <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">
        universal suffrage
       </a>
       was introduced in 1906, the parliament has been dominated by the
       <a href="/wiki/Centre_Party_(Finland)" title="Centre Party (Finland)">
        Centre Party
       </a>
       (former Agrarian Union), the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Coalition_Party" title="National Coalition Party">
        National Coalition Party
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Finland" title="Social Democratic Party of Finland">
        Social Democrats
       </a>
       . These parties have enjoyed approximately equal support, and their combined vote has totalled about 65–80% of all votes. Their lowest common total of MPs, 121, was reached in the 2011 elections. For a few decades after 1944, the
       <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Finland" title="Communist Party of Finland">
        Communists
       </a>
       were a strong fourth party. Due to the electoral system of proportional representation, and the relative reluctance of voters to switch their support between parties, the relative strengths of the parties have commonly varied only slightly from one election to another. However, there have been some long-term trends, such as the rise and fall of the Communists during the Cold War; the steady decline into insignificance of the
       <a href="/wiki/Liberals_(Finland)" title="Liberals (Finland)">
        Liberals
       </a>
       and its predecessors from 1906 to 1980; and the rise of the
       <a href="/wiki/Green_League" title="Green League">
        Green League
       </a>
       since 1983. In the 2011 elections, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/True_Finns" title="True Finns">
        Finns Party
       </a>
       achieved exceptional success, increasing its representation from 5 to 39 seats, surpassing the Centre Party.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The autonomous province of Åland, which forms a
       <a href="/wiki/Federacy" title="Federacy">
        federacy
       </a>
       with Finland, elects one member to the parliament, who traditionally joins the
       <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_group" title="Parliamentary group">
        parliamentary group
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Swedish_People%27s_Party_of_Finland" title="Swedish People's Party of Finland">
        Swedish People's Party of Finland
       </a>
       . (The province also holds elections for its own permanent
       <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_%C3%85land" title="Parliament of Åland">
        regional council
       </a>
       , and in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C3%85land_legislative_election,_2011" title="Åland legislative election, 2011">
        2011 elections
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/%C3%85land_Centre" title="Åland Centre">
        Åland Centre
       </a>
       was the largest party.)
      </p>
      <table class="vertical-navbox vcard" style="float:right;clear:right;width:22.0em;margin:0 0 1.0em 1.0em;background:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;padding:0.2em;border-spacing:0.4em 0;text-align:center;line-height:1.4em;font-size:88%;width:19.5em;">
       <tr>
        <th style="padding:0.2em 0.4em 0.2em;font-size:145%;line-height:1.2em">
         <div class="adr" style="font-size:smaller">
          <span class="fn org country-name">
           <a class="mw-selflink selflink">
            Republic of Finland
           </a>
          </span>
         </div>
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th>
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_arms_of_Finland.svg">

         </a>
        </th>
       </tr>

            </li>

      <p>
       The Parliament can be dissolved by a recommendation of the Prime Minister, endorsed by the President. This procedure has never been used, although the parliament was dissolved eight times under the pre-2000 constitution, when this action was the sole prerogative of the president.
      </p>
