      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cabinet">
        Cabinet
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Cabinet">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Female_Cabinet_Ministers_in_Finland" title="List of Female Cabinet Ministers in Finland">
        List of Female Cabinet Ministers in Finland
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       After parliamentary elections, the parties negotiate among themselves on forming a new cabinet (the
       <a href="/wiki/Finnish_Government" title="Finnish Government">
        Finnish Government
       </a>
       ), which then has to be approved by a simple majority vote in the parliament. The cabinet can be dismissed by a parliamentary vote of no confidence, although this rarely happens (the last time in 1957), as the parties represented in the cabinet usually make up a majority in the parliament.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The cabinet exercises most executive powers, and originates most of the bills that the parliament then debates and votes on. It is headed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Finland" title="Prime Minister of Finland">
        Prime Minister of Finland
       </a>
       , and consists of him or her, of other ministers, and of the
       <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_Justice#Finland" title="Chancellor of Justice">
        Chancellor of Justice
       </a>
       . The current prime minister is
       <a href="/wiki/Juha_Sipil%C3%A4" title="Juha Sipilä">
        Juha Sipilä
       </a>
       (Centre Party). Each minister heads his or her ministry, or, in some cases, has responsibility for a subset of a ministry's policy. After the prime minister, the most powerful minister is the
       <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_Finance_(Finland)" title="Minister of Finance (Finland)">
        minister of finance
       </a>
       . The incumbent Minister of Finance is
       <a href="/wiki/Petteri_Orpo" title="Petteri Orpo">
        Petteri Orpo
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       As no one party ever dominates the parliament, Finnish cabinets are multi-party coalitions. As a rule, the post of prime minister goes to the leader of the biggest party and that of the minister of finance to the leader of the second biggest.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Law">
        Law
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Law">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Finland" title="Law of Finland">
        Law of Finland
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Judicial_system_of_Finland" title="Judicial system of Finland">
        Judicial system of Finland
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The judicial system of Finland is a
       <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">
        civil law
       </a>
       system divided between
       <a href="/wiki/Court" title="Court">
        courts
       </a>
       with regular civil and criminal jurisdiction and
       <a href="/wiki/Administrative_court" title="Administrative court">
        administrative courts
       </a>
       with jurisdiction over litigation between individuals and the public administration. Finnish law is codified and based on
       <a href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_Sweden" title="Judiciary of Sweden">
        Swedish law
       </a>
       and in a wider sense, civil law or
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_law" title="Roman law">
        Roman law
       </a>
       . The court system for civil and criminal jurisdiction consists of local courts (
       <i>
        käräjäoikeus
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        tingsrätt
       </i>
       ), regional appellate courts (
       <i>
        hovioikeus
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        hovrätt
       </i>
       ), and the
       <a href="/wiki/Judicial_system_of_Finland#Supreme_Court" title="Judicial system of Finland">
        Supreme Court
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        korkein oikeus
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        högsta domstolen
       </i>
       ). The administrative branch of justice consists of administrative courts (
       <i>
        hallinto-oikeus
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        förvaltningsdomstol
       </i>
       ) and the
       <a href="/wiki/Judicial_system_of_Finland#Supreme_Administrative_Court" title="Judicial system of Finland">
        Supreme Administrative Court
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        korkein hallinto-oikeus
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        högsta förvaltningsdomstolen
       </i>
       ). In addition to the regular courts, there are a few special courts in certain branches of administration. There is also a
       <a href="/wiki/Judicial_system_of_Finland#High_Court_of_Impeachment" title="Judicial system of Finland">
        High Court of Impeachment
       </a>
       for criminal charges against certain high-ranking officeholders.
      </p>
      <p>
       Around 92% of residents have confidence in Finland's security institutions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-corruptionpolicing_87-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-corruptionpolicing-87">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The overall
       <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Finland" title="Crime in Finland">
        crime rate of Finland
       </a>
       is not high in the EU context. Some crime types are above average, notably the highest
       <a href="/wiki/Homicide" title="Homicide">
        homicide
       </a>
       rate in Western Europe.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eucrime_88-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-eucrime-88">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Day_fine" title="Day fine">
        day fine
       </a>
       system is in effect and also applied to offenses such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Speeding" title="Speeding">
        speeding
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Finland has successfully fought against government corruption, which was more common in the 1970s and 80s.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-corruption_89-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-corruption-89">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
          <span title="The material near this tag needs to be fact-checked with the cited source(s). (March 2011)">
           verification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       For instance, economic reforms and EU membership introduced stricter requirements for open bidding and many public monopolies were abolished.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-corruption_89-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-corruption-89">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Today, Finland has a very low number of corruption charges;
       <a href="/wiki/Transparency_International" title="Transparency International">
        Transparency International
       </a>
       ranks Finland as one of the least corrupt countries in Europe.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2008, Transparency International criticized the lack of transparency of the system of Finnish political finance.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
        <a href="#cite_note-90">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to
       <a href="/wiki/Group_of_States_Against_Corruption" title="Group of States Against Corruption">
        GRECO
       </a>
       in 2007, corruption should be taken into account in the Finnish system of election funds better.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2007_campaign_finance_scandal_of_Finland" title="2007 campaign finance scandal of Finland">
        A scandal revolving around campaign finance of the 2007 parliamentary elections
       </a>
       broke out in spring 2008. Nine Ministers of Government submitted incomplete funding reports and even more of the members of parliament. The law includes no punishment of false funds reports of the elected politicians.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">
        Foreign relations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Finland" title="Foreign relations of Finland">
        Foreign relations of Finland
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nobel_Peace_Prize_2008_Martti_Ahtisaari.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="320" height="413" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Nobel_Peace_Prize_2008_Martti_Ahtisaari.jpg/220px-Nobel_Peace_Prize_2008_Martti_Ahtisaari.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/49/Nobel_Peace_Prize_2008_Martti_Ahtisaari.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nobel_Peace_Prize_2008_Martti_Ahtisaari.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Martti_Ahtisaari" title="Martti Ahtisaari">
          Martti Ahtisaari
         </a>
         receiving the Nobel Peace Prize in 2008
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       According to the 2012 constitution, the president (currently
       <a href="/wiki/Sauli_Niinist%C3%B6" title="Sauli Niinistö">
        Sauli Niinistö
       </a>
       ) leads foreign policy in cooperation with the government, except that the president has no role in EU affairs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Finnish_constitution._92-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Finnish_constitution.-92">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2008, president
       <a href="/wiki/Martti_Ahtisaari" title="Martti Ahtisaari">
        Martti Ahtisaari
       </a>
       was awarded the
       <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">
        Nobel Peace Prize
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nobelprize_93-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Nobelprize-93">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Finland was considered a cooperative model state, and Finland did not oppose proposals for a common EU defence policy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-foreignpolicyidea_94-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-foreignpolicyidea-94">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This was reversed in the 2000s, when Tarja Halonen and
       <a href="/wiki/Erkki_Tuomioja" title="Erkki Tuomioja">
        Erkki Tuomioja
       </a>
       made Finland's official policy to resist other EU members' plans for common defence.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-foreignpolicyidea_94-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-foreignpolicyidea-94">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Social_security">
        Social security
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Social security">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_security_in_Finland" title="Social security in Finland">
        Social security in Finland
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Finland has one of the world's most extensive welfare systems, one that guarantees decent living conditions for all residents, Finns, and non-citizens. Since the 1980s the social security has been cut back, but still the system is one of the most comprehensive in the world. Created almost entirely during the first three decades after World War II, the social security system was an outgrowth of the traditional Nordic belief that the state was not inherently hostile to the well-being of its citizens, but could intervene benevolently on their behalf. According to some social historians, the basis of this belief was a relatively benign history that had allowed the gradual emergence of a free and independent peasantry in the Nordic countries and had curtailed the dominance of the nobility and the subsequent formation of a powerful right wing. Finland's history has been harsher than the histories of the other Nordic countries, but not harsh enough to bar the country from following their path of social development.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_95-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-LOC-95">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Military">
        Military
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Military">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tracked_transport_vehicle_Sisu_NA_110.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="1024" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Tracked_transport_vehicle_Sisu_NA_110.JPG/220px-Tracked_transport_vehicle_Sisu_NA_110.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Tracked_transport_vehicle_Sisu_NA_110.JPG/330px-Tracked_transport_vehicle_Sisu_NA_110.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Tracked_transport_vehicle_Sisu_NA_110.JPG/440px-Tracked_transport_vehicle_Sisu_NA_110.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tracked_transport_vehicle_Sisu_NA_110.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Sisu_Nasu" title="Sisu Nasu">
          Sisu Nasu
         </a>
         NA-110 tracked transport vehicle of the Finnish Army. Most conscripts receive training for warfare in winter, and transport vehicles such as this give mobility in heavy snow.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Finnish_Defence_Forces" title="Finnish Defence Forces">
        Finnish Defence Forces
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Finland" title="Military history of Finland">
        Military history of Finland
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_wars_involving_Finland" title="List of wars involving Finland">
        List of wars involving Finland
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Finnish Defence Forces consist of a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/En_cadre" title="En cadre">
        cadre
       </a>
       of professional soldiers (mainly officers and technical personnel), currently serving conscripts, and a large reserve. The standard readiness strength is 34,700 people in uniform, of which 25% are professional soldiers. A universal male
       <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">
        conscription
       </a>
       is in place, under which all male Finnish nationals above 18 years of age serve for 6 to 12 months of armed service or 12 months of civilian (non-armed) service. Voluntary post-conscription overseas peacekeeping service is popular, and troops serve around the world in UN, NATO, and EU missions. Approximately 500 women choose voluntary military service every year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Women are allowed to serve in all combat arms including front-line infantry and special forces. The army consists of a highly mobile field army backed up by local defence units. The army defends the national territory and its military strategy employs the use of the heavily forested terrain and numerous lakes to wear down an aggressor, instead of attempting to hold the attacking army on the frontier.
      </p>
      <p>
       Finnish defence expenditure per capita is one of the highest in the European Union.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
        <a href="#cite_note-97">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Finnish military doctrine is based on the concept of total defence. The term total means that all sectors of the government and economy are involved in the defence planning. The armed forces are under the command of the
       <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_Defence_(Finland)" title="Chief of Defence (Finland)">
        Chief of Defence
       </a>
       (currently General
       <a href="/wiki/Jarmo_Lindberg" title="Jarmo Lindberg">
        Jarmo Lindberg
       </a>
       ), who is directly subordinate to the president in matters related to military command. The branches of the military are the
       <a href="/wiki/Finnish_Army" title="Finnish Army">
        army
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Finnish_Navy" title="Finnish Navy">
        navy
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Finnish_Air_Force" title="Finnish Air Force">
        air force
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Finnish_Border_Guard" title="Finnish Border Guard">
        border guard
       </a>
       is under the Ministry of the Interior but can be incorporated into the Defence Forces when required for defence readiness.
      </p>
      <p>
       Even while Finland hasn't joined the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Treaty_Organization" title="North Atlantic Treaty Organization">
        North Atlantic Treaty Organization
       </a>
       , the country has joined the
       <a href="/wiki/NATO_Response_Force" title="NATO Response Force">
        NATO Response Force
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/EU_Battlegroup" title="EU Battlegroup">
        EU Battlegroup
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       the NATO
       <a href="/wiki/Partnership_for_Peace" title="Partnership for Peace">
        Partnership for Peace
       </a>
       and in signed a NATO
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Memorandum_of_Understanding" title="Memorandum of Understanding">
        Memorandum of Understanding
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eduskunta.fi_98-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-eduskunta.fi-98">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
       thus forming a practical coalition.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nato.int_18-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-nato.int-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2015, the Finland-NATO ties were strengthened with a host nation support agreement allowing assistance from NATO troops in emergency situations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
        <a href="#cite_note-99">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Finland has been active participant in the Afghanistan and Kosovo.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
        <a href="#cite_note-100">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
        <a href="#cite_note-101">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Recently Finland has been more eager to discuss about its current and planned roles in Syria, Iraq and war against ISIL.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
        <a href="#cite_note-102">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On 21 December 2012 Finnish military officer
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Atte_Kaleva&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Atte Kaleva (page does not exist)">
        Atte Kaleva
       </a>
       was reported to have been kidnapped and later released in Yemen for ransom. At first he was reported be a casual Arabic student, however only later it was published that his studies were about jihadists, terrorism, and that he was employed by the military.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
        <a href="#cite_note-103">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
        <a href="#cite_note-104">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As response to French request for solidarity, Finnish defence minister commented in November that Finland could and is willing to offer intelligence support.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
        <a href="#cite_note-105">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In May 2015, Finnish Military sent nearly one million letters to all relevant males in the country, informing them about their roles in the war effort. It was globally speculated that Finland was preparing for war—however Finland claimed that this was a standard procedure, yet something never done before in Finnish history.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibtimes.com_106-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ibtimes.com-106">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Mr Hypponen however said that this is not an isolated case, but bound to the European security dilemma.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibtimes.com_106-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ibtimes.com-106">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The NATO Memorandum of Understanding signed earlier bestows an obligation e.g. to report on internal capabilities and the availability thereof to NATO.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eduskunta.fi_98-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-eduskunta.fi-98">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Angry_Birds_Land_S%C3%A4rk%C3%A4nniemi_11.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Angry_Birds_Land_S%C3%A4rk%C3%A4nniemi_11.jpg/220px-Angry_Birds_Land_S%C3%A4rk%C3%A4nniemi_11.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Angry_Birds_Land_S%C3%A4rk%C3%A4nniemi_11.jpg/330px-Angry_Birds_Land_S%C3%A4rk%C3%A4nniemi_11.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Angry_Birds_Land_S%C3%A4rk%C3%A4nniemi_11.jpg/440px-Angry_Birds_Land_S%C3%A4rk%C3%A4nniemi_11.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Angry_Birds_Land_S%C3%A4rk%C3%A4nniemi_11.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Angry_Birds" title="Angry Birds">
          Angry Birds
         </a>
         , a mobile phone game developed in Finland, has become a commercial hit both domestically and internationally.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Finland" title="Economy of Finland">
        Economy of Finland
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_of_Finland" title="List of companies of Finland">
        List of companies of Finland
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Helsinki_Stock_Exchange" title="Helsinki Stock Exchange">
        Helsinki Stock Exchange
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The economy of Finland has a per capita output equal to that of other European economies such as those of France, Germany,
       <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">
        Belgium
       </a>
       , or the UK. The largest sector of the economy is the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Service_sector" title="Service sector">
        service sector
       </a>
       at 66% of GDP, followed by manufacturing and refining at 31%.
       <a href="/wiki/Primary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Primary sector of the economy">
        Primary production
       </a>
       represents 2.9%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
        <a href="#cite_note-107">
         [106]
        </a>
       </sup>
       With respect to
       <a href="/wiki/International_trade" title="International trade">
        foreign trade
       </a>
       , the key economic sector is manufacturing. The largest industries in 2007
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
        <a href="#cite_note-108">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
       were
       <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">
        electronics
       </a>
       (22%); machinery, vehicles, and other engineered metal products (21.1%); forest industry (13%); and chemicals (11%). The gross domestic product peaked in 2008. As of 2015
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , the country's economy is at the 2006 level.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
        <a href="#cite_note-109">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
        <a href="#cite_note-110">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Finland has significant timber, mineral (
       <a href="/wiki/Iron" title="Iron">
        iron
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Chromium" title="Chromium">
        chromium
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">
        copper
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nickel" title="Nickel">
        nickel
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">
        gold
       </a>
       ), and freshwater resources.
       <a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">
        Forestry
       </a>
       , paper factories, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">
        agricultural sector
       </a>
       (on which taxpayers spend
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (June 2017)">
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       around 3 billion euros annually) are important for rural residents so any policy changes affecting these sectors are politically sensitive for politicians dependent on rural votes. The
       <a href="/wiki/Greater_Helsinki" title="Greater Helsinki">
        Greater Helsinki
       </a>
       area generates around one third of Finland's GDP. In a 2004 OECD comparison, high-technology manufacturing in Finland ranked second largest after Ireland. Knowledge-intensive services have also resulted in the smallest and slow-growth sectors – especially agriculture and low-technology manufacturing – being ranked the second largest after Ireland.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oecd2004_111-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-oecd2004-111">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The overall short-term outlook was good and GDP growth has been above that of many EU peers.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Image_illustrates_GDP_growth_of_Finland.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="289" data-file-width="566" height="112" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/5b/Image_illustrates_GDP_growth_of_Finland.png/220px-Image_illustrates_GDP_growth_of_Finland.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/5b/Image_illustrates_GDP_growth_of_Finland.png/330px-Image_illustrates_GDP_growth_of_Finland.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/5b/Image_illustrates_GDP_growth_of_Finland.png/440px-Image_illustrates_GDP_growth_of_Finland.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Image_illustrates_GDP_growth_of_Finland.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Finland GDP growth from 2000 till 2013
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Finland is highly integrated into the global economy, and international trade produces one third of GDP. Trade with the European Union makes up 60% of Finland's total trade. The largest trade flows are with Germany, Russia, Sweden, the United Kingdom, the United States, the
       <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">
        Netherlands
       </a>
       , and China. Trade policy is managed by the European Union, where Finland has traditionally been among the free trade supporters, except for agricultural policy. Finland is the only Nordic country to have joined the Eurozone.
      </p>
      <p>
       Finland's climate and soils make growing crops a particular challenge. The country lies between the latitudes 60°N and 70°N, and it has severe winters and relatively short growing seasons that are sometimes interrupted by frost. However, because the Gulf Stream and the North Atlantic Drift Current moderate the climate, Finland contains half of the world's arable land north of 60° north latitude. Annual precipitation is usually sufficient, but it occurs almost exclusively during the winter months, making summer droughts a constant threat. In response to the climate, farmers have relied on quick-ripening and frost-resistant varieties of crops, and they have cultivated south-facing slopes as well as richer bottomlands to ensure production even in years with summer frosts. Most farmland was originally either forest or swamp, and the soil has usually required treatment with lime and years of cultivation to neutralize excess acid and to improve fertility. Irrigation has generally not been necessary, but drainage systems are often needed to remove excess water. Finland's agriculture has been efficient and productive—at least when compared with farming in other European countries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_95-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-LOC-95">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Forests play a key role in the country's economy, making it one of the world's leading wood producers and providing raw materials at competitive prices for the crucial wood-processing industries. As in agriculture, the government has long played a leading role in forestry, regulating tree cutting, sponsoring technical improvements, and establishing long-term plans to ensure that the country's forests continue to supply the wood-processing industries. To maintain the country's comparative advantage in forest products, Finnish authorities moved to raise lumber output toward the country's ecological limits. In 1984, the government published the Forest 2000 plan, drawn up by the Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry. The plan aimed at increasing forest harvests by about 3% per year, while conserving forestland for recreation and other uses.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_95-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-LOC-95">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Private sector employees amount to 1.8 million, out of which around a third with tertiary education. The average cost of a private sector employee per hour was 25.1 euros in 2004.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
        <a href="#cite_note-112">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As of 2008
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , average purchasing power-adjusted income levels are similar to those of Italy, Sweden, Germany, and France.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-incomecomparison_113-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-incomecomparison-113">
         [112]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2006, 62% of the workforce worked for enterprises with less than 250 employees and they accounted for 49% of total business turnover and had the strongest rate of growth.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
        <a href="#cite_note-114">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The female employment rate is high. Gender segregation between male-dominated professions and female-dominated professions is higher than in the US.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-niels_115-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-niels-115">
         [114]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The proportion of part-time workers was one of the lowest in OECD in 1999.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-niels_115-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-niels-115">
         [114]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2013, the 10 largest private sector employers in Finland were
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Itella" title="Itella">
        Itella
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nokia" title="Nokia">
        Nokia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/OP_Financial_Group" title="OP Financial Group">
        OP-Pohjola
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/ISS_A/S" title="ISS A/S">
        ISS
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VR_Group" title="VR Group">
        VR
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kesko" title="Kesko">
        Kesko
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UPM-Kymmene" title="UPM-Kymmene">
        UPM-Kymmene
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/YIT" title="YIT">
        YIT
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Metso" title="Metso">
        Metso
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Nordea" title="Nordea">
        Nordea
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
        <a href="#cite_note-116">
         [115]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The unemployment rate was 9.4% in 2015, having risen from 8.7% in 2014.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
        <a href="#cite_note-117">
         [116]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Youth unemployment rate rose from 16.5% in 2007 to 20.5% in 2014.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
        <a href="#cite_note-118">
         [117]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A fifth of residents are outside the job market at the age of 50 and less than a third are working at the age of 61.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
        <a href="#cite_note-119">
         [118]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As of today, nearly one million people are living with minimal wages or unemployed not enough to cover their costs of living.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
        <a href="#cite_note-120">
         [119]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As of 2006
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , 2.4 million households reside in Finland. The average size is 2.1 persons; 40% of households consist of a single person, 32% two persons and 28% three or more persons. Residential buildings total 1.2 million, and the average residential space is 38 square metres (410 sq ft) per person. The average residential property without land costs 1,187 euro per sq metre and residential land 8.6 euro per sq metre. 74% of households had a car. There are 2.5 million cars and 0.4 million other vehicles.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
        <a href="#cite_note-121">
         [120]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Around 92% have a mobile phone and 83.5% (2009)
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_number_of_Internet_users" title="List of countries by number of Internet users">
        Internet connection at home
       </a>
       . The average total household consumption was 20,000 euro, out of which housing consisted of about 5,500 euro, transport about 3,000 euro, food and beverages excluding alcoholic beverages at around 2,500 euro, and recreation and culture at around 2,000 euro.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
        <a href="#cite_note-122">
         [121]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to Invest in Finland, private consumption grew by 3% in 2006 and consumer trends included durables, high quality products, and spending on well-being.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
        <a href="#cite_note-123">
         [122]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">
        Energy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Energy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EPR_OLK3_TVO_fotomont_2_Vogelperspektive.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1000" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/EPR_OLK3_TVO_fotomont_2_Vogelperspektive.jpg/220px-EPR_OLK3_TVO_fotomont_2_Vogelperspektive.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/EPR_OLK3_TVO_fotomont_2_Vogelperspektive.jpg/330px-EPR_OLK3_TVO_fotomont_2_Vogelperspektive.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/EPR_OLK3_TVO_fotomont_2_Vogelperspektive.jpg/440px-EPR_OLK3_TVO_fotomont_2_Vogelperspektive.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EPR_OLK3_TVO_fotomont_2_Vogelperspektive.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The two existing units of the
         <a href="/wiki/Olkiluoto_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Olkiluoto Nuclear Power Plant">
          Olkiluoto Nuclear Power Plant
         </a>
         . On the far left is a visualization of a third unit, which, when completed, will become Finland's fifth commercial nuclear reactor.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-olkiluoto_delayed_124-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-olkiluoto_delayed-124">
           [123]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Nordic_energy_market" title="Nordic energy market">
        Nordic energy market
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_in_Finland" title="Nuclear power in Finland">
        Nuclear power in Finland
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The free and largely privately owned financial and physical
       <a href="/wiki/Nordic_energy_market" title="Nordic energy market">
        Nordic energy markets
       </a>
       traded in
       <a href="/wiki/NASDAQ_OMX_Commodities_Europe" title="NASDAQ OMX Commodities Europe">
        NASDAQ OMX Commodities Europe
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nord_Pool_Spot" title="Nord Pool Spot">
        Nord Pool Spot
       </a>
       exchanges, have provided competitive prices compared with other EU countries. As of 2007
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , Finland has roughly the lowest industrial electricity prices in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EU-15" title="EU-15">
        EU-15
       </a>
       (equal to France).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
        <a href="#cite_note-125">
         [124]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2006, the energy market was around 90 terawatt hours and the peak demand around 15
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gigawatt" title="Gigawatt">
        gigawatts
       </a>
       in winter. This means that the
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_energy_consumption_per_capita" title="List of countries by energy consumption per capita">
        energy consumption per capita
       </a>
       is around 7.2 tons of oil equivalent per year. Industry and construction consumed 51% of total consumption, a relatively high figure reflecting Finland's industries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
        <a href="#cite_note-126">
         [125]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
        <a href="#cite_note-127">
         [126]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Finland's
       <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon" title="Hydrocarbon">
        hydrocarbon
       </a>
       resources are limited to
       <a href="/wiki/Peat" title="Peat">
        peat
       </a>
       and wood. About 10–15% of the electricity is produced by
       <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">
        hydropower
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
        <a href="#cite_note-128">
         [127]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which is low compared with more mountainous Sweden or Norway. In 2008,
       <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">
        renewable energy
       </a>
       (mainly hydropower and various forms of wood energy) was high at 31% compared with the EU average of 10.3% in final energy consumption.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">
        <a href="#cite_note-129">
         [128]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Statistics_of_the_energy_supply_in_Finland.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="324" data-file-width="723" height="99" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b8/Statistics_of_the_energy_supply_in_Finland.jpg/220px-Statistics_of_the_energy_supply_in_Finland.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b8/Statistics_of_the_energy_supply_in_Finland.jpg/330px-Statistics_of_the_energy_supply_in_Finland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b8/Statistics_of_the_energy_supply_in_Finland.jpg/440px-Statistics_of_the_energy_supply_in_Finland.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Statistics_of_the_energy_supply_in_Finland.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Supply and total consumption of electricity in Finland
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Statistics_Finland,_Energy_130-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-Statistics_Finland,_Energy-130">
           [129]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Finland has four privately owned nuclear reactors producing 18% of the country's energy
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">
        <a href="#cite_note-131">
         [130]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and one research reactor at the
       <a href="/wiki/Otaniemi" title="Otaniemi">
        Otaniemi
       </a>
       campus. The fifth
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AREVA" title="AREVA">
        AREVA
       </a>
       -
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siemens_AG" title="Siemens AG">
        Siemens
       </a>
       -built reactor—the world's largest at 1600
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MWe" title="MWe">
        MWe
       </a>
       and a focal point of Europe's nuclear industry—has faced many delays and is currently scheduled to be operational by 2018–2020, a decade after the original planned opening.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kauppalehti-02-2014_132-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-kauppalehti-02-2014-132">
         [131]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A varying amount (5–17%) of electricity has been imported from Russia (at around 3 gigawatt power line capacity), Sweden and Norway.
      </p>
      <p>
       Energy companies are about to increase nuclear power production, as in July 2010 the Finnish parliament granted permits for additional two new reactors.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">
        Transport
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Transport">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Finland" title="Transport in Finland">
        Transport in Finland
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kontio_towing.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Kontio_towing.jpg/220px-Kontio_towing.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Kontio_towing.jpg/330px-Kontio_towing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Kontio_towing.jpg/440px-Kontio_towing.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kontio_towing.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Icebreaker" title="Icebreaker">
          Icebreakers
         </a>
         enable shipping even during severe winters.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:I1949_Bf_B%C3%B6le,_Sr2_3220.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2912" data-file-width="4368" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/I1949_Bf_B%C3%B6le%2C_Sr2_3220.jpg/220px-I1949_Bf_B%C3%B6le%2C_Sr2_3220.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/I1949_Bf_B%C3%B6le%2C_Sr2_3220.jpg/330px-I1949_Bf_B%C3%B6le%2C_Sr2_3220.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/I1949_Bf_B%C3%B6le%2C_Sr2_3220.jpg/440px-I1949_Bf_B%C3%B6le%2C_Sr2_3220.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:I1949_Bf_B%C3%B6le,_Sr2_3220.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The state-owned
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VR_Group" title="VR Group">
          VR Group
         </a>
         operates a railway network serving all major cities.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The extensive road system is utilized by most internal cargo and passenger traffic. The annual state operated road network expenditure of around 1 billion euro is paid with vehicle and fuel taxes which amount to around 1.5 billion euro and 1 billion euro.
      </p>
      <p>
       The main international passenger gateway is
       <a href="/wiki/Helsinki_Airport" title="Helsinki Airport">
        Helsinki Airport
       </a>
       with about 17 million passengers in 2016.
       <a href="/wiki/Oulu_Airport" title="Oulu Airport">
        Oulu Airport
       </a>
       is the second largest, whilst another
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Finland" title="List of airports in Finland">
        25 airports
       </a>
       have scheduled passenger services.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-finavia_pass_stats_133-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-finavia_pass_stats-133">
         [132]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Helsinki Airport-based
       <a href="/wiki/Finnair" title="Finnair">
        Finnair
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Blue1" title="Blue1">
        Blue1
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Regional_Airlines" title="Nordic Regional Airlines">
        Nordic Regional Airlines
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Air_Shuttle" title="Norwegian Air Shuttle">
        Norwegian Air Shuttle
       </a>
       sell air services both domestically and internationally. Helsinki has an optimal location for
       <a href="/wiki/Great_circle" title="Great circle">
        great circle
       </a>
       (i.e. the shortest and most efficient) routes between Western Europe and the Far East.
      </p>
      <p>
       Despite low population density, the Government spends annually around 350 million euro in maintaining 5,865 kilometres (3,644 mi) of railway tracks. Rail transport is handled by state owned
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VR_Group" title="VR Group">
        VR Group
       </a>
       , which has 5% passenger market share (out of which 80% are urban trips in Greater Helsinki) and 25% cargo market share.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ljvr_134-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ljvr-134">
         [133]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Since 12 December 2010,
       <a href="/wiki/Karelian_Trains" title="Karelian Trains">
        Karelian Trains
       </a>
       , a joint venture between
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Railways" title="Russian Railways">
        Russian Railways
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VR_Group" title="VR Group">
        VR (Finnish Railways)
       </a>
       , has been running
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Karelian_Trains_Class_Sm6" title="Karelian Trains Class Sm6">
        Alstom Pendolino
       </a>
       operated high-speed services between Saint Petersburg's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Finlyandsky_Rail_Terminal" title="Finlyandsky Rail Terminal">
        Finlyandsky
       </a>
       and Helsinki's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Helsinki_Central_railway_station" title="Helsinki Central railway station">
        Central
       </a>
       railway stations. These services are branded as "Allegro" trains. The journey from Helsinki to
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">
        Saint Petersburg
       </a>
       takes only three and a half hours.
      </p>
      <p>
       The majority of international cargo utilizes ports. Port logistics prices are low.
       <a href="/wiki/Vuosaari_Harbour" title="Vuosaari Harbour">
        Vuosaari Harbour
       </a>
       in Helsinki is the largest container port after completion in 2008 and others include
       <a href="/wiki/Kotka" title="Kotka">
        Kotka
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hamina" title="Hamina">
        Hamina
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hanko" title="Hanko">
        Hanko
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pori" title="Pori">
        Pori
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Rauma,_Finland" title="Rauma, Finland">
        Rauma
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Oulu" title="Oulu">
        Oulu
       </a>
       . There is passenger traffic from Helsinki and Turku, which have ferry connections to
       <a href="/wiki/Tallinn" title="Tallinn">
        Tallinn
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mariehamn" title="Mariehamn">
        Mariehamn
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">
        Stockholm
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Travem%C3%BCnde" title="Travemünde">
        Travemünde
       </a>
       . The Helsinki-Tallinn route, one of the busiest passenger sea routes in the world, has also been served by a helicopter line.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Industry">
        Industry
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Industry">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Finland" title="Economy of Finland">
        Economy of Finland
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Finnair,_Airbus_A350-900_OH-LWC_NRT_(30222794141).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3485" data-file-width="5227" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Finnair%2C_Airbus_A350-900_OH-LWC_NRT_%2830222794141%29.jpg/220px-Finnair%2C_Airbus_A350-900_OH-LWC_NRT_%2830222794141%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Finnair%2C_Airbus_A350-900_OH-LWC_NRT_%2830222794141%29.jpg/330px-Finnair%2C_Airbus_A350-900_OH-LWC_NRT_%2830222794141%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Finnair%2C_Airbus_A350-900_OH-LWC_NRT_%2830222794141%29.jpg/440px-Finnair%2C_Airbus_A350-900_OH-LWC_NRT_%2830222794141%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Finnair,_Airbus_A350-900_OH-LWC_NRT_(30222794141).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Finnair" title="Finnair">
          Finnair
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A350_XWB" title="Airbus A350 XWB">
          Airbus A350 XWB
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Finland was rapidly industrialized after World War II, achieving GDP per capita levels equal to that of Japan or the UK in the beginning of the 1970s. Initially, most development was based on two broad groups of export-led industries, the "metal industry" (
       <i>
        metalliteollisuus
       </i>
       ) and "forest industry" (
       <i>
        metsäteollisuus
       </i>
       ). The "metal industry" includes shipbuilding, metalworking, the car industry, engineered products such as motors and electronics, and production of metals (steel, copper and chromium). The world's biggest
       <a href="/wiki/Cruise_ship" title="Cruise ship">
        cruise ships
       </a>
       are built in Finnish shipyards. The "forest industry" (
       <i>
        metsäteollisuus
       </i>
       ) includes forestry, timber, pulp and paper, and is a logical development based on Finland's extensive forest resources (77% of the area is covered by forest, most of it in renewable use). In the
       <a href="/wiki/Pulp_and_paper_industry" title="Pulp and paper industry">
        pulp and paper industry
       </a>
       , many of the largest companies are based in Finland (
       <a href="/wiki/Ahlstrom" title="Ahlstrom">
        Ahlstrom
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mets%C3%A4_Board" title="Metsä Board">
        Metsä Board
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/UPM_(company)" title="UPM (company)">
        UPM
       </a>
       ). However, the Finnish economy has diversified, with expansion into fields such as electronics (e.g.
       <a href="/wiki/Nokia" title="Nokia">
        Nokia
       </a>
       ), metrology (
       <a href="/wiki/Vaisala" title="Vaisala">
        Vaisala
       </a>
       ), transport fuels (
       <a href="/wiki/Neste" title="Neste">
        Neste
       </a>
       ), chemicals (
       <a href="/wiki/Kemira" title="Kemira">
        Kemira
       </a>
       ), engineering consulting (
       <a href="/wiki/P%C3%B6yry" title="Pöyry">
        Pöyry
       </a>
       ), and information technology (e.g.
       <a href="/wiki/Rovio_Entertainment" title="Rovio Entertainment">
        Rovio Entertainment
       </a>
       , known for
       <a href="/wiki/Angry_Birds" title="Angry Birds">
        Angry Birds
       </a>
       ), and is no longer dominated by the two sectors of metal and forest industry. Likewise, the structure has changed, with the service sector growing, with manufacturing reducing in importance; agriculture is only a minor part. Despite this, production for export is still more prominent than in Western Europe, thus making Finland more vulnerable to global economic trends.
      </p>
      <p>
       In an
       <a href="/wiki/Economist_Intelligence_Unit" title="Economist Intelligence Unit">
        Economist Intelligence Unit
       </a>
       report released in September 2011, Finland clinched the second place after the United States on Benchmarking IT Industry Competitiveness 2011 which scored on 6 key indicators: overall business environment, technology infrastructure, human capital, legal framework, public support for industry development, and research and development landscape.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">
        <a href="#cite_note-135">
         [134]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Public_policy">
        Public policy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Public policy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Nordic_model" title="Nordic model">
        Nordic model
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Finnish politicians have often emulated other Nordics and the Nordic model.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nordicmodel_136-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-nordicmodel-136">
         [135]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Nordics have been free-trading and relatively welcoming to skilled migrants for over a century, though in Finland
       <a href="/wiki/Immigration" title="Immigration">
        immigration
       </a>
       is relatively new. The level of protection in commodity trade has been low, except for agricultural products.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nordicmodel_136-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-nordicmodel-136">
         [135]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Finland has top levels of economic freedom in many areas.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2011)">
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Finland is ranked 16th in the 2008 global
       <a href="/wiki/Index_of_Economic_Freedom" title="Index of Economic Freedom">
        Index of Economic Freedom
       </a>
       and 9th in Europe.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-freedom_137-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-freedom-137">
         [136]
        </a>
       </sup>
       While the manufacturing sector is thriving, the OECD points out that the service sector would benefit substantially from policy improvements.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">
        <a href="#cite_note-138">
         [137]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The 2007
       <a href="/wiki/International_Institute_for_Management_Development" title="International Institute for Management Development">
        IMD
       </a>
       World Competitiveness Yearbook ranked Finland 17th most
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Competitiveness" title="Competitiveness">
        competitive
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">
        <a href="#cite_note-139">
         [138]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">
        World Economic Forum
       </a>
       2008 index ranked Finland the 6th most competitive.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">
        <a href="#cite_note-140">
         [139]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In both indicators, Finland's performance was next to Germany, and significantly higher than most European countries. In the Business competitiveness index 2007–2008 Finland ranked third in the world.
      </p>
      <p>
       Economists attribute much growth to reforms in the product markets. According to the OECD, only four
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EU-15" title="EU-15">
        EU-15
       </a>
       countries have less regulated
       <a href="/wiki/Product_market" title="Product market">
        product markets
       </a>
       (UK, Ireland, Denmark and Sweden) and only one has less regulated
       <a href="/wiki/Financial_market" title="Financial market">
        financial markets
       </a>
       (Denmark). Nordic countries were pioneers in liberalizing energy, postal, and other markets in Europe.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nordicmodel_136-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-nordicmodel-136">
         [135]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The legal system is clear and business bureaucracy less than most countries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-freedom_137-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-freedom-137">
         [136]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Property rights are well protected and contractual agreements are strictly honoured.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-freedom_137-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-freedom-137">
         [136]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Finland is rated the least corrupt country in the world in the
       <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index" title="Corruption Perceptions Index">
        Corruption Perceptions Index
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">
        <a href="#cite_note-141">
         [140]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and 13th in the
       <a href="/wiki/Ease_of_doing_business_index" title="Ease of doing business index">
        Ease of doing business index
       </a>
       . This indicates exceptional ease in cross-border trading (5th), contract enforcement (7th), business closure (5th), tax payment (83rd), and low worker hardship (127th).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">
        <a href="#cite_note-142">
         [141]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Finnish law
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universal_validity_of_collective_labour_agreements" title="Universal validity of collective labour agreements">
        forces all workers to obey the national contracts
       </a>
       that are drafted every few years for each profession and seniority level. The agreement becomes universally enforceable provided that more than 50% of the employees support it, in practice by being a member of a relevant trade union. The unionization rate is high (70%), especially in the middle class (
       <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_Unions_for_Academic_Professionals_in_Finland" title="Confederation of Unions for Academic Professionals in Finland">
        AKAVA
       </a>
       —80%). A lack of a national agreement in an industry is considered an exception.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oecd2004_111-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-oecd2004-111">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nordicmodel_136-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-nordicmodel-136">
         [135]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rovaniemi_pajakyla.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Rovaniemi_pajakyla.jpg/220px-Rovaniemi_pajakyla.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Rovaniemi_pajakyla.jpg/330px-Rovaniemi_pajakyla.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Rovaniemi_pajakyla.jpg/440px-Rovaniemi_pajakyla.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rovaniemi_pajakyla.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Santa_Claus" title="Santa Claus">
          Santa Claus
         </a>
         village in Rovaniemi.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">
        Tourism
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Tourism">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Finland" title="Tourism in Finland">
        Tourism in Finland
       </a>
      </div>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           does not
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
            cite
           </a>
           any
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            sources
           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit">

           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">
            adding citations to reliable sources
           </a>
           . Unsourced material may be challenged and
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">

           </a>
           .
          </span>

            (July 2017)
           </i>
