         <a href="/wiki/IIHF_World_Ranking" title="IIHF World Ranking">
          ranked
         </a>
         as one of the best in the world. The team has won two world championship titles (in 1995 &amp; 2011) and six Olympic medals.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Finland" title="Sport in Finland">
        Sport in Finland
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Various sporting events are popular in Finland.
       <a href="/wiki/Pes%C3%A4pallo" title="Pesäpallo">
        Pesäpallo
       </a>
       , resembling baseball, is the national sport of Finland, although the most popular sports in terms of spectators is
       <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">
        ice hockey
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/2016_IIHF_World_Championship" title="2016 IIHF World Championship">
        Ice Hockey World Championships 2016
       </a>
       final Finland-Canada, 69% Finnish people watched that game on TV.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198">
        <a href="#cite_note-198">
         [197]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Other popular sports include
       <a href="/wiki/Track_and_field" title="Track and field">
        athletics
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cross-country_skiing" title="Cross-country skiing">
        cross-country skiing
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ski_jumping" title="Ski jumping">
        ski jumping
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">
        football
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">
        basketball
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199">
        <a href="#cite_note-199">
         [198]
        </a>
       </sup>
       While ice hockey is the most popular sports when it comes to attendance at games,
       <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">
        association football
       </a>
       is the most played team sport in terms of the amount of players in the country and is also the most appreciated sports in Finland.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200">
        <a href="#cite_note-200">
         [199]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201">
        <a href="#cite_note-201">
         [200]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In terms of medals and gold medals won per capita, Finland is the best performing country in Olympic history.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202">
        <a href="#cite_note-202">
         [201]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Finland first participated as a nation in its own right at the
       <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">
        Olympic Games
       </a>
       in 1908, while still an autonomous
       <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Finland" title="Grand Duchy of Finland">
        Grand Duchy
       </a>
       within the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">
        Russian Empire
       </a>
       . At the
       <a href="/wiki/1912_Summer_Olympics" title="1912 Summer Olympics">
        1912 Summer Olympics
       </a>
       , great pride was taken in the three gold medals won by the original "
       <a href="/wiki/Flying_Finn" title="Flying Finn">
        Flying Finn
       </a>
       "
       <a href="/wiki/Hannes_Kolehmainen" title="Hannes Kolehmainen">
        Hannes Kolehmainen
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Finland was one of the most successful countries at the Olympic Games before
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
        World War II
       </a>
       . At the
       <a href="/wiki/1924_Summer_Olympics" title="1924 Summer Olympics">
        1924 Summer Olympics
       </a>
       , Finland, a nation then of only 3.2 million people, came second in the medal count. In the 1920s and 1930s, Finnish long-distance runners dominated the Olympics, with
       <a href="/wiki/Paavo_Nurmi" title="Paavo Nurmi">
        Paavo Nurmi
       </a>
       winning a total of nine Olympic gold medals between 1920 and 1928 and setting 22 official world records between 1921 and 1931. Nurmi is often considered the greatest Finnish sportsman and one of the greatest athletes of all time.
      </p>
      <p>
       For over 100 years, Finnish male and female athletes have consistently excelled at the
       <a href="/wiki/Javelin_throw" title="Javelin throw">
        javelin throw
       </a>
       . The event has brought Finland nine Olympic gold medals, five world championships, five European championships, and 24 world records.
      </p>
      <p>
       In addition to Kolehmainen and Nurmi, some of Finland's most internationally well-known and successful sportspeople are long-distance runners
       <a href="/wiki/Ville_Ritola" title="Ville Ritola">
        Ville Ritola
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Lasse_Vir%C3%A9n" title="Lasse Virén">
        Lasse Virén
       </a>
       ; ski-jumpers
       <a href="/wiki/Matti_Nyk%C3%A4nen" title="Matti Nykänen">
        Matti Nykänen
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Janne_Ahonen" title="Janne Ahonen">
        Janne Ahonen
       </a>
       ; cross-country skiers
       <a href="/wiki/Veikko_Hakulinen" title="Veikko Hakulinen">
        Veikko Hakulinen
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Eero_M%C3%A4ntyranta" title="Eero Mäntyranta">
        Eero Mäntyranta
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Marja-Liisa_Kirvesniemi" title="Marja-Liisa Kirvesniemi">
        Marja-Liisa Kirvesniemi
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mika_Myllyl%C3%A4" title="Mika Myllylä">
        Mika Myllylä
       </a>
       ; rower
       <a href="/wiki/Pertti_Karppinen" title="Pertti Karppinen">
        Pertti Karppinen
       </a>
       ; gymnast
       <a href="/wiki/Heikki_Savolainen_(gymnast)" title="Heikki Savolainen (gymnast)">
        Heikki Savolainen
       </a>
       ; professional skateboarder
       <a href="/wiki/Arto_Saari" title="Arto Saari">
        Arto Saari
       </a>
       ; ice hockey players
       <a href="/wiki/Kimmo_Timonen" title="Kimmo Timonen">
        Kimmo Timonen
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jari_Kurri" title="Jari Kurri">
        Jari Kurri
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Teemu_Sel%C3%A4nne" title="Teemu Selänne">
        Teemu Selänne
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Saku_Koivu" title="Saku Koivu">
        Saku Koivu
       </a>
       ; football players
       <a href="/wiki/Jari_Litmanen" title="Jari Litmanen">
        Jari Litmanen
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Sami_Hyypi%C3%A4" title="Sami Hyypiä">
        Sami Hyypiä
       </a>
       ; basketball player
       <a href="/wiki/Hanno_M%C3%B6tt%C3%B6l%C3%A4" title="Hanno Möttölä">
        Hanno Möttölä
       </a>
       ; alpine skiers
       <a href="/wiki/Kalle_Palander" title="Kalle Palander">
        Kalle Palander
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tanja_Poutiainen" title="Tanja Poutiainen">
        Tanja Poutiainen
       </a>
       ; Formula One world champions
       <a href="/wiki/Keke_Rosberg" title="Keke Rosberg">
        Keke Rosberg
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mika_H%C3%A4kkinen" title="Mika Häkkinen">
        Mika Häkkinen
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Kimi_R%C3%A4ikk%C3%B6nen" title="Kimi Räikkönen">
        Kimi Räikkönen
       </a>
       ; four-time World Rally champions
       <a href="/wiki/Juha_Kankkunen" title="Juha Kankkunen">
        Juha Kankkunen
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tommi_M%C3%A4kinen" title="Tommi Mäkinen">
        Tommi Mäkinen
       </a>
       ; and 13-time World
       <a href="/wiki/Enduro" title="Enduro">
        Enduro
       </a>
       Champion
       <a href="/wiki/Juha_Salminen" title="Juha Salminen">
        Juha Salminen
       </a>
       , seven-time champion
       <a href="/wiki/Kari_Tiainen" title="Kari Tiainen">
        Kari Tiainen
       </a>
       , and the five-time champions
       <a href="/wiki/Mika_Ahola" title="Mika Ahola">
        Mika Ahola
       </a>
       , biathlete
       <a href="/wiki/Kaisa_M%C3%A4k%C3%A4r%C3%A4inen" title="Kaisa Mäkäräinen">
        Kaisa Mäkäräinen
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Samuli_Aro" title="Samuli Aro">
        Samuli Aro
       </a>
       . Finland is also one of the most successful nations in
       <a href="/wiki/Bandy" title="Bandy">
        bandy
       </a>
       , being the only nation beside Russia and Sweden to win a
       <a href="/wiki/Bandy_World_Championship" title="Bandy World Championship">
        Bandy World Championship
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/1952_Summer_Olympics" title="1952 Summer Olympics">
        1952 Summer Olympics
       </a>
       were held in Helsinki. Other notable sporting events held in Finland include the
       <a href="/wiki/1983_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="1983 World Championships in Athletics">
        1983
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/2005_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="2005 World Championships in Athletics">
        2005 World Championships in Athletics
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Finland also has a notable history in
       <a href="/wiki/Figure_skating" title="Figure skating">
        figure skating
       </a>
       . Finnish skaters have won 8 world championships and 13 junior world cups in synchronized skating, and Finland is considered one of the best countries at the sport.
      </p>
      <p>
       Some of the most popular recreational sports and activities include
       <a href="/wiki/Floorball" title="Floorball">
        floorball
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nordic_walking" title="Nordic walking">
        Nordic walking
       </a>
       , running, cycling, and skiing (
       <a href="/wiki/Alpine_skiing" title="Alpine skiing">
        alpine skiing
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cross-country_skiing" title="Cross-country skiing">
        cross-country skiing
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Ski_jumping" title="Ski jumping">
        ski jumping
       </a>
       ). Floorball, in terms of registered players, occupies third place after football and ice hockey. According to the Finnish Floorball Federation, floorball is the most popular school, youth, club and workplace sport.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203">
        <a href="#cite_note-203">
         [202]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As of 2016, the total number of licensed players reaches 57,400.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204">
        <a href="#cite_note-204">
         [203]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Especially since the
       <a href="/wiki/2014_FIBA_Basketball_World_Cup" title="2014 FIBA Basketball World Cup">
        2014 FIBA Basketball World Cup
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Finland_national_basketball_team" title="Finland national basketball team">
        Finland's national basketball team
       </a>
       has received widespread public attention. More than 8,000 Finns travelled to Spain to support their team. Overall, they chartered more than 40 airplanes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205">
        <a href="#cite_note-205">
         [204]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">
        Notes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Notes">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references">
         <li id="cite_note-65">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-65">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           The names for Finland in its Sami languages are:
           <i>
            Suopma
           </i>
           (
           <a href="/wiki/Northern_Sami" title="Northern Sami">
            Northern Sami
           </a>
           ),
           <i>
            Suomâ
           </i>
           (
           <a href="/wiki/Inari_Sami_language" title="Inari Sami language">
            Inari Sami
           </a>
           ) and
           <i>
            Lää´ddjânnam
           </i>
           (
           <a href="/wiki/Skolt_Sami_language" title="Skolt Sami language">
            Skolt Sami
           </a>
           ). See
           <a class="external text" href="http://www.geonames.de/coufi.html" rel="nofollow">
            Geonames.de
           </a>
           .
          </span>
         </li>
        </ol>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="References">
        References
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Finland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: References">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">
       <ol class="references">
        <li id="cite_note-Parliamentary-1">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          ^
          <a href="#cite_ref-Parliamentary_1-0">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              a
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-Parliamentary_1-1">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              b
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          Formerly a semi-presidential republic, it is now a parliamentary republic according to David Arter, First Chair of Politics at Aberdeen University. In his "Scandinavian Politics Today" (Manchester University Press, revised 2008
          <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
           ISBN
          </a>
          <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780719078538" title="Special:BookSources/9780719078538">
           9780719078538
          </a>
          ), he quotes
          <cite class="citation journal" id="CITEREFNousiainen2001">
           Nousiainen, Jaakko (June 2001).
           <a class="external text" href="https://dx.doi.org/10.1111/1467-9477.00048" rel="nofollow">
            "From semi-presidentialism to parliamentary government: political and constitutional developments in Finland"
           </a>
           .
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Political_Studies" title="Scandinavian Political Studies">
             Scandinavian Political Studies
            </a>
           </i>
           .
           <a href="/wiki/Wiley-Blackwell" title="Wiley-Blackwell">
            Wiley
           </a>
           .
           <b>
            24
           </b>
           (2): 95–109.
           <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">
            doi
           </a>
           :
           <a class="external text" href="//doi.org/10.1111%2F1467-9477.00048" rel="nofollow">
            10.1111/1467-9477.00048
           </a>
           .
          </cite>
          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Scandinavian+Political+Studies&amp;rft.atitle=From+semi-presidentialism+to+parliamentary+government%3A+political+and+constitutional+developments+in+Finland&amp;rft.volume=24&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.pages=95-109&amp;rft.date=2001-06&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1111%2F1467-9477.00048&amp;rft.aulast=Nousiainen&amp;rft.aufirst=Jaakko&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fdx.doi.org%2F10.1111%2F1467-9477.00048&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFinland">
           <span style="display:none;">
           </span>
          </span>
          as follows: "There are hardly any grounds for the epithet 'semi-presidential'." Arter's own conclusions are only slightly more nuanced: "The adoption of a new constitution on 1 March 2000 meant that Finland was no longer a case of semi-presidential government other than in the minimalist sense of a situation where a popularly elected fixed-term president exists alongside a prime minister and cabinet who are responsible to parliament (Elgie 2004: 317)". According to the Finnish Constitution, the president has no possibility to rule the government without the ministerial approval, and does not have the power to dissolve the parliament under his or her own desire. Finland is actually represented by its prime minister, and not by its president, in the Council of the Heads of State and Government of the European Union. The 2012 constitutional amendments reduced the powers of the president even further.
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-2">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-2">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>

          <cite class="citation web">

            "Finland's preliminary population figure 5,509,717 at the end of August"
           </a>

           <i>

           </span>

          <i>
           <span lang="se">
            Suoma dásseváldi
           </span>
          </i>
          " in Sami, is the long protocol name, which is however not defined by law. Legislation recognises only the short name.

        <li id="cite_note-full_suffrage-17">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-full_suffrage_17-0">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          Finland was the first nation in the world to give all (adult) citizens full suffrage, in other words the right to vote and to run for office, in 1906. New Zealand was the first country in the world to grant all (adult) citizens the right to vote, in 1893. But women did not get the right to run for the New Zealand legislature, until 1919.
         </span>

               <div>
                <div class="plainlist">
                 <ul>
                  <li>
                   <sup>
                    1
                   </sup>
                   <a href="/wiki/Island#Oceanic_islands" title="Island">
                    Oceanic islands
                   </a>
                   within the vicinity of Europe are usually grouped with the continent even though they are not situated on its continental shelf.
                  </li>

                   <sup>
                    2
                   </sup>
                   Some countries completely outside the conventional geographical boundaries of Europe are commonly associated with the continent due to ethnological links.
